        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789896411732" href="/book/show/17231888-cem-poemas">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6923777-teresa?shelf=g-poesia">g-poesia</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer631628016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6598114978946881420">Como todas as minhas palavras de amor para Dickinson serão ridículas (obrigada Álvaro de Campos), transcrevo as de Bloom — e as Dela.<br/><br/><i>"A força da sua poesia é indubitável, como a da Bíblia, de Shakespeare, de Blake e de Whitman. Apenas se irá tornar um desafio cada vez maior à medida que passem os séculos. Como Whitman, ela há-de deter-se algures, à nossa espera."</i><br/>Harold Bloom<br/>______________________________<br/>"Mostrei-lhe Cumes que ela nunca vira —<br/>«Sobes?», disse eu<br/>Ela disse — «Não» —<br/>«<i>Comigo</i>» — disse </span>
  <span id="freeText6598114978946881420" style="display:none">Como todas as minhas palavras de amor para Dickinson serão ridículas (obrigada Álvaro de Campos), transcrevo as de Bloom — e as Dela.<br /><br /><i>"A força da sua poesia é indubitável, como a da Bíblia, de Shakespeare, de Blake e de Whitman. Apenas se irá tornar um desafio cada vez maior à medida que passem os séculos. Como Whitman, ela há-de deter-se algures, à nossa espera."</i><br />Harold Bloom<br />______________________________<br />"Mostrei-lhe Cumes que ela nunca vira —<br />«Sobes?», disse eu<br />Ela disse — «Não» —<br />«<i>Comigo</i>» — disse eu — <i>Comigo</i>?<br />Mostrei-lhe Segredos — o Ninho da Manhã —<br />A Corda que as Noites estenderam —<br />E <i>agora</i> — «Convidas-me a ficar?»<br />Ela não soube bem se dizer Sim —<br />E então, eu afrouxei a minha vida — E<br />Para ela, ali brilhou solene, a Luz,<br />Tão mais quanto mais longe a sua face —<br /><i>Como</i> podia ela, ainda, dizer «Não»?"<br />______________________________<br />"A Dor — tem um Elemento de Branco —<br />Não consegue lembrar <br />O seu início — ou se existiu<br />Um tempo em que não foi —<br /><br />Não tem Futuro — só em si —<br />O Sem Fim contém <br />O seu Passado — pronto a discernir<br />Novos Períodos — de Dor."<br />_____________________________<br />"Dizem que o «Tempo acalma» —<br />Nunca o tempo acalmou —<br />A dor real é que se faz mais tensa<br />Como os Tendões, com a idade —<br /><br />O Tempo é uma Prova de Tormento —<br />Mas não o seu Remédio —<br />E se tal coisa prova, também prova<br />Que não houve Doença —"<br />______________________________<br /><br />Cem poemas a ler...<blockquote>"Para sempre — é composto de Agoras —<br />Não é um tempo diferente —<br />Excepto pela Infinidade —<br />E Latitude de Lar —<br /><br />Disto — Aqui experimentado —<br />Tirem-se a Estes — as Datas —<br />Que os Meses se dissolvam noutros Meses —<br />E os Anos — se dissipem noutros Anos —<br /><br />Sem Debate — nem Pausa —<br />Nem Feriado a Cumprir —<br />Não seriam diferentes os Nossos Anos <br />Do <i>Anno Domini</i> —"</blockquote> ...para sempre —<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6598114978946881420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2037671756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2037671756" />
    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037671756?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K. Elizabeth" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth">K. Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=very-good-but-not-phenomenal">very-good-but-not-phenomenal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037671756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15828964403400132200"><b>4 stars</b><br/><br/>After reading through most of these poems, Emily remains one of my top favorite poets. However, I also came across <i>many</i> poems that I felt no connection with and frankly made no sense to me. So with that in mind, I unfortunately couldn't give this 5 stars. Still a great experience though! <br/><br/>I highly recommend this book if you're a fan of poetry and/or Emily Dickinson.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Dan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10770371-dan"><img alt="Dan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540580928p2/10770371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2901260693?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan" href="/user/show/10770371-dan">Dan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2901260693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16880412064489300373"><b>Twas such a little, little boat<br/>That toddled down the bay!<br/>‘T was such a gallant, gallant sea<br/>That beckoned it away!<br/><br/>‘T was such a greedy, greedy wave<br/>That licked it from the coast;<br/>Nor ever guessed the stately sails<br/>My little craft was lost!<\b><br/><br/>Or this one, <b><br/><br/>The morns are meeker than they were,<br/>The nuts are getting brown;<br/>“The berry’s cheek is plumper,<br/>The rose is out of town.<br/><br/>The maple wears a gayer scarf,<br/>The field a scarlet gown.<br/>Lest I should be old-fashioned,<br/>I’ll put a trinket on.<\b><br/><br/>Immeasurable and pr</b></b></span>
  <span id="freeText16880412064489300373" style="display:none"><b>Twas such a little, little boat<br />That toddled down the bay!<br />‘T was such a gallant, gallant sea<br />That beckoned it away!<br /><br />‘T was such a greedy, greedy wave<br />That licked it from the coast;<br />Nor ever guessed the stately sails<br />My little craft was lost!&lt;\b&gt;<br /><br />Or this one, <b><br /><br />The morns are meeker than they were,<br />The nuts are getting brown;<br />“The berry’s cheek is plumper,<br />The rose is out of town.<br /><br />The maple wears a gayer scarf,<br />The field a scarlet gown.<br />Lest I should be old-fashioned,<br />I’ll put a trinket on.&lt;\b&gt;<br /><br />Immeasurable and prolific Emily Dickinson wrote nearly 2,000 poems. Upon reading this complete collection it is remarkable the sheer amount of beautiful opening lines, certainly more than any other poet that I’ve read. Dickinson’s poems are typically very short and heavily metaphorical. <br /><br />Dickinson’s great gifts are that of a consummate observer — both of nature and of her immediate environment — and her propensity to draw metaphors. Her observations in many poems deal with the theme of depression. Dickinson we know was a bit of a hermit. She also was not really much of a story teller in the usual sense since she wrote no epic length poems. But her poetry holds up well considering most were penned prior to 1850. Since Dickinson did not provide titles for most of her poems editors often name the poem after the first line. I have followed their standard here. Here are my favorites. All are in the public domain. <br /><br />1. Unreturning<br />2. The Brain within its Groove<br />3. A Service of Song<br />4. A Day<br />5. Autumn<br />6. I’m nobody, who are you?<br />7. In the Garden<br />8. November<br />9. I felt a funeral in my brain<br />10. Dead<br />11. Charlotte Bronte’s Grave<br />12. Nobody Knows this Little Rose<br />13. I fear a man of frugal speech<br />14. I never saw a moor<br />15. Dear March, Come In<br />16. Tis easier to pity those when dead<br /><br />4.5 stars. </b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16880412064489300373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_4826696" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4826696" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/237437-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410835759p2/237437.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4826696?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/237437-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/237437-diana?shelf=readingallthetime">readingallthetime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4826696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17200743219685032831">I love Dickinson. More specifically, I love the sense of balance I feel when reading any of her poems. Her poetry has light within its overwhelming darkness; it is straightforward yet subtle. Its originality is sometimes even startling. I have learned so much in reading her work but the most powerful of lessons I take from Dickinson is to "Tell all the truth but tell it slant... The Truth must dazzle gradually/ Or every man be blind."</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1710473658" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1710473658" />
    <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour"><img alt="J.M. Hushour" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442964894p2/17463213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1710473658?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.M. Hushour" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour">J.M. Hushour</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316184410" href="/book/show/149307.The_Complete_Poems_of_Emily_Dickinson">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710473658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8122866993278875856">Running upwards of 1,700 poems, there's no conceivable way I could read them all. I settled for maybe half. That's not to say I'm not tempted to read them all, but Dickinson is one of those fine poets who begin to run a little stale after the first 200 or so poems. Best to step off and return to it later.<br/>Don't get me wrong, her innovative poetics is almost ghastly in its profundity, so much so that people use words like 'profundity' or say that she, who had no powers of prescience that her biogr</span>
  <span id="freeText8122866993278875856" style="display:none">Running upwards of 1,700 poems, there's no conceivable way I could read them all. I settled for maybe half. That's not to say I'm not tempted to read them all, but Dickinson is one of those fine poets who begin to run a little stale after the first 200 or so poems. Best to step off and return to it later.<br />Don't get me wrong, her innovative poetics is almost ghastly in its profundity, so much so that people use words like 'profundity' or say that she, who had no powers of prescience that her biographers are aware of, 'anticipated modernity', whatever that means. That means nothing. We don't need to place her. I think she was beyond that. Still is. Her poetry is almost drunken--staccato and broken and weird and refusing. In short, wonderful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8122866993278875856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369225571" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1369225571?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Flexibound 9781626863897" href="/book/show/23168273-the-poetry-of-emily-dickinson">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369225571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5655745271312060059">The first time I consciously had contact with Emily Dickinson's poetry was when author and illustrator Chris Riddell posted one of his beautiful sketches on facebook decorating one of her poems. After that I knew I had to have a collection of her works.<br/><br/>Then I discovered the World Cloud Classics and it was the perfect edition in my opinion (this being the 3rd I have now).<br/><br/>I must say that I love poetry, always have, and although I don't always favour the kind of analysis being done in school (we al</span>
  <span id="freeText5655745271312060059" style="display:none">The first time I consciously had contact with Emily Dickinson's poetry was when author and illustrator Chris Riddell posted one of his beautiful sketches on facebook decorating one of her poems. After that I knew I had to have a collection of her works.<br><br>Then I discovered the World Cloud Classics and it was the perfect edition in my opinion (this being the 3rd I have now).<br><br>I must say that I love poetry, always have, and although I don't always favour the kind of analysis being done in school (we all had to get through <i>that</i>), I do see and acknowledge autobiographical elements in works.<br>Here, as with Walt Whitman for example, it is remarkable that isolation and sickness resulted in the most fruitful creative period. What always gets to me is the tragedy of such lives and that in many cases (as with Emily Dickinson) none or only a handful of the works were being published / recognized while the author was alive, the true impact and significance of the works to be discovered only later.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440243629i/15951666._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now for the poems themselves:<br>Amazing as it might be considering that the author spent almost all of her life indoors, her poems are of a wide range. Not actually knowing much of the world around her didn't stop her from writing about it (her favourite themes being nature and love, death and immortality, but also renunciation).<br>The prose is beautiful, I have no other word for it. To me it seemed like she must have been a quiet person but very intelligent and with powerful words; everyday-words artfully crafted into profound messages. I guess that is what I love so much about her.<br><br>Example:<br><br> „To make a prairie it takes a clover and a bee,<br> one clover, and a bee,<br> And revery.<br> The revery alone will do,<br> If bees are few.”<br><br>One of my teachers once said "The shorter the story, the more important every single word." and Emily Dickinson is proving that. Another example of a short poem that still has full impact:<br><br> "A word is dead<br> When it is said,<br> Some say -<br> <br> I say it just<br> Begins to live<br> That day."<br><br>Or:<br><br> "I never saw a moor,<br> I never saw the sea,<br> Yet know I how the Heather looks<br> And what a wave must be."<br><br>I could have included all those poems as pictures but somehow enjoyed tiping them myself. Yeah, I'm weird like that. Also, I could go on like this forever since there wasn't a single poem I really disliked, but the following one shall conclude my review since you are probably all getting my point. It's the poem docarated by Chris Riddell's illustration that started it all.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440243629i/15951667.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5655745271312060059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=america-fuck-yeah">america-fuck-yeah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=poesy">poesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=femmes">femmes</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40362694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18299978660400055282"><br/> I've read a fair bit of her poetry and all I can say is that it astounds me, seduces me, challenges me, enlightens me.<br/><br/> I can't lay claim to being any kind of expert but I love her vision, her way of seeing, her developing a highly idiosyncratic personal language that is informed by previous poetic tradition but that resolutely bends the note and pushes it forward. "Making it new" before it was cool, before they even had a name for it. I'm actually kind of hesitant to read more of her because I </span>
  <span id="freeText18299978660400055282" style="display:none"><br /> I've read a fair bit of her poetry and all I can say is that it astounds me, seduces me, challenges me, enlightens me.<br /><br /> I can't lay claim to being any kind of expert but I love her vision, her way of seeing, her developing a highly idiosyncratic personal language that is informed by previous poetic tradition but that resolutely bends the note and pushes it forward. "Making it new" before it was cool, before they even had a name for it. I'm actually kind of hesitant to read more of her because I think I'm not ready yet...her power is exhausting and exhaustive...</span>
  <a data-text-id="18299978660400055282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264651?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristopher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristopher" href="/user/show/84658-kristopher">Kristopher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Poetry lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84658-kristopher?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84658-kristopher?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84658-kristopher?shelf=collections">collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84658-kristopher?shelf=formative">formative</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16275894851118967798">I would highly, highly recommend strolling through Dickinson's collected verse. She's a (surprisingly) highly underrated poet. Going deep into her entire collection will unearth unknown gems as well as old favorites. This edition, organized chronologically, allows the opportunity to study her growth as a poet and explore her obsessions over time. It also provides the date of first publication (if there was one). A must-have for any poetry enthusiast, highly recommended for those who have a modes</span>
  <span id="freeText16275894851118967798" style="display:none">I would highly, highly recommend strolling through Dickinson's collected verse. She's a (surprisingly) highly underrated poet. Going deep into her entire collection will unearth unknown gems as well as old favorites. This edition, organized chronologically, allows the opportunity to study her growth as a poet and explore her obsessions over time. It also provides the date of first publication (if there was one). A must-have for any poetry enthusiast, highly recommended for those who have a modest interest in poetry since it collects all of the poetry of one of America's most influential, accessible, and subtly complex poets.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16275894851118967798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LuYakBSBwbVPCBJV5O+jjGQuHxuPt8lIbA/ngb9X3Aw0FZ7guyg26TSDtcfUI9go8cfAP5X/GaHA/pH6K/joTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XjDV+98F8TPtieOoMo9m26JsugUX0yvlTW3oDEeYL9ZEw1GLcKwGb5YCRDoCQx1/N4VlIQ2b+wzhnJ530zcblg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7440.Emily_Dickinson">About Emily Dickinson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7440.Emily_Dickinson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1198536260p3/7440.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7440.Emily_Dickinson">Emily Dickinson
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,738
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13703538723485942496">Emily Dickinson was an American poet who, despite the fact that less than a dozen of her nearly eighteen hundred poems were published during her lifetime, is widely considered one of the most original and influential poets of the 19th century.<br/><br/>Dickinson was born to a successful family with strong community ties, she lived a mostly introverted and reclusive life. After she studied at the Amherst Aca</span>
  <span id="freeText13703538723485942496" style="display:none">Emily Dickinson was an American poet who, despite the fact that less than a dozen of her nearly eighteen hundred poems were published during her lifetime, is widely considered one of the most original and influential poets of the 19th century.<br /><br />Dickinson was born to a successful family with strong community ties, she lived a mostly introverted and reclusive life. After she studied at the Amherst Academy for seven years in her youth, she spent a short time at Mount Holyoke Female Seminary before returning to her family's house in Amherst. Thought of as an eccentric by the locals, she became known for her penchant for white clothing and her reluctance to greet guests or, later in life, even leave her room. Most of her friendships were therefore carried out by correspondence.<br /><br />Although Dickinson was a prolific private poet, fewer than a dozen of her nearly eighteen hundred poems were published during her lifetime.The work that was published during her lifetime was usually altered significantly by the publishers to fit the conventional poetic rules of the time. Dickinson's poems are unique for the era in which she wrote; they contain short lines, typically lack titles, and often use slant rhyme as well as unconventional capitalization and punctuation.Many of her poems deal with themes of death and immortality, two recurring topics in letters to her friends.<br /><br />Although most of her acquaintances were probably aware of Dickinson's writing, it was not until after her death in 1886—when Lavinia, Emily's younger sister, discovered her cache of poems—that the breadth of Dickinson's work became apparent. Her first collection of poetry was published in 1890 by personal acquaintances Thomas Wentworth Higginson and Mabel Loomis Todd, both of whom heavily edited the content. <br /><br />A complete and mostly unaltered collection of her poetry became available for the first time in 1955 when The Poems of Emily Dickinson was published by scholar Thomas H. Johnson. Despite unfavorable reviews and skepticism of her literary prowess during the late 19th and early 20th century, critics now consider Dickinson to be a major American poet.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.answers.com/topic/emily-dickinson">http://www.answers.com/topic/emily-di...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13703538723485942496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I'm nobody! Who are you? <br />Are you nobody, too? <br />Then there ’s a pair of us—don’t tell! <br />They ’d banish us, you know. <br /> <br />How dreary to be somebody! <br />How public, like a frog <br />To tell your name the livelong day <br />To an admiring bog!&rdquo;</span>
